842

843 <section id="_387">

844

845 <h2>

846General Information about Late Effects</h2>

847

848 <div id="_section_387" class="pdq-sections">

849<div class="pdq-hp-patient-toggle">

850<a href="/types/childhood-cancers/late-effects-hp-pdq">

851Go to Health Professional Version</a>

852</div>

853<div class="key-points">

854<h3 id="_387_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

855Key Points</h3>

856<div id="_kp_section_387_1">

857<ul>

858<li>

859Late effects are health problems that occur months or years after cancer treatment has ended.</li>

860<li>

861Late effects in childhood cancer survivors affect the body and mind.</li>

862<li>

863There are three important factors that affect the risk of late effects. </li>

864<li>

865The chance of having late effects increases over time.</li>

866<li>

867Regular follow-up care is very important for survivors of childhood cancer.</li>

868<li>

869Good health habits are also important for survivors of childhood cancer.</li>

870</ul>

871</div>

872</div>

873<section id="_485">

874<h3 id="_486" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

875Late effects are health problems that occur months or years after cancer treatment has ended.</h3>

876<p id="_566" tabindex="-1">

877Cancer treatments may harm the body's <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

878organs</a>

879, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

880tissues</a>

881, or bones and cause health problems later in life. These health problems are called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=390292&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000390292&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

882late effects</a>

883. </p>

884<p id="_956" tabindex="-1">

885Treatments that may cause late effects include the following:</p>

886<div class="pdq-content-list">

887<ul id="_944">

888<li>

889<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

890Surgery</a>

891.</li>

892<li>

893<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45214&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045214&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

894Chemotherapy</a>

895.</li>

896<li>

897<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44971&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044971&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

898Radiation therapy</a>

899.</li>

900<li>

901<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46695&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046695&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

902Stem cell transplant</a>

903.</li>

904</ul>

905</div>

906<p id="_395" tabindex="-1">

907Doctors are studying the late effects caused by cancer treatment. They are working to improve cancer treatments and stop or lessen late effects. While most late effects are not life-threatening, they may cause serious problems that affect health and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45417&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045417&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

908quality of life</a>

909.</p>

910</section>

911<section id="_391">

912<h3 id="_392" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

913Late effects in childhood cancer survivors affect the body and mind.</h3>

914<p id="_520" tabindex="-1">

915Late effects in childhood cancer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=450125&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000450125&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

916survivors</a>

917 may affect the following:</p>

918<div class="pdq-content-list">

919<ul id="_393">

920<li>

921Organs, tissues, and body function.</li>

922<li>

923Growth and development.</li>

924<li>

925Mood, feelings, and actions. </li>

926<li>

927Thinking, learning, and memory. </li>

928<li>

929Social and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=454766&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000454766&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

930psychological</a>

931 adjustment.</li>

932<li>

933Risk of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46658&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046658&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

934second cancers</a>

935.</li>

936</ul>

937</div>

938</section>

939<section id="_523">

940<h3 id="_524" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

941There are three important factors that affect the risk of late effects. </h3>

942<p id="_533" tabindex="-1">

943Many childhood cancer survivors will have late effects. The risk of late effects depends on factors related to the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

944tumor</a>

945, treatment, and patient. These include the following:</p>

946<div class="pdq-content-list">

947<ul id="_534">

948<li>

949<strong>

950Tumor-related factors</strong>

951<div class="pdq-content-list">

952<ul id="_535" class="list-dash">

953<li>

954Type of cancer.</li>

955<li>

956Where the tumor is in the body.</li>

957<li>

958How the tumor affects the way tissues and organs work.</li>

959</ul>

960</div>

961</li>

981<li>

1034</section>

1035<section id="_381">

1036<h3 id="_382" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1037The chance of having late effects increases over time.</h3>

1038<p id="_383" tabindex="-1">

1039New treatments for childhood cancer have decreased the number of deaths from the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45847&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045847&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1040primary cancer</a>

1041. Because childhood cancer survivors are living longer, they are having more late effects after cancer treatment. Survivors may not live as long as people who did not have cancer. The most common causes of death in childhood cancer survivors are:</p>

1042<div class="pdq-content-list">

1043<ul id="_19">

1044<li>

1045The primary cancer comes back.</li>

1046<li>

1047A second (different) primary cancer forms.</li>

1048<li>

1049Heart and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1050lung</a>

1051 damage.</li>

1052</ul>

1053</div>

1054<p id="_20" tabindex="-1">

1055<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44195&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044195&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1056Studies</a>

1057 of the causes of late effects have led to changes in treatment. This has improved the quality of life for cancer survivors and helps <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=439419&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000439419&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1058prevent</a>

1059 illness and death from late effects.

1060

1061</p>

1062</section>

1063<section id="_27">

1064<h3 id="_28" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1065Regular follow-up care is very important for survivors of childhood cancer.</h3>

1066<p id="_567" tabindex="-1">

1067Regular <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1068follow-up</a>

1069 by health professionals who are trained to find and treat late effects is important for the long-term health of childhood cancer survivors. Follow-up care will be different for each person who has been treated for cancer. The type of care will depend on the type of cancer, the type of treatment, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46391&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046391&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1070genetic</a>

1071 factors, other medical conditions, and the person's general health and health habits. Follow-up care includes checking for <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1072signs</a>

1073 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1074symptoms</a>

1075 of late effects and health education on how to prevent or lessen late effects.</p>

1076<p id="_568" tabindex="-1">

1077It is important that childhood cancer survivors have an exam at least once a year. The exams should be done by a health professional who knows the survivor's risk for late effects and can recognize the early signs of late effects. Blood and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=689578&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000689578&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1078imaging tests</a>

1079 may also be done.</p>

1080<p id="_32" tabindex="-1">

1081Long-term follow-up may improve the health and quality of life for cancer survivors. It also helps doctors study the late effects of cancer treatments so that safer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44737&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044737&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1082therapies</a>

1083 for newly diagnosed children may be developed. </p>

1084</section>

1085<section id="_526">

1086<h3 id="_527" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1087Good health habits are also important for survivors of childhood cancer.</h3>

1088<p id="_528" tabindex="-1">

1089The quality of life for cancer survivors may be improved by behaviors that promote health and well-being. These include a healthy <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44660&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044660&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1090diet</a>

1091, exercise, and regular medical and dental checkups. These self-care behaviors are especially important for cancer survivors because of their risk of health problems related to treatment. Healthy behaviors may make late effects less severe and lower the risk of other diseases.</p>

1092<p id="_529" tabindex="-1">

1093Avoiding behaviors that are damaging to health is also important. Smoking, excess <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=463134&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000463134&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1094alcohol</a>

1095 use, illegal <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=348921&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000348921&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1096drug</a>

1097 use, being exposed to sunlight, or not being physically active may worsen organ damage related to treatment and may increase the risk of second cancers.</p>

1098</section>

1099</div>

1100

1101 </section>

1105 <section id="_36">

1106

1107 <h2>

1108Second Cancers</h2>

1109

1110 <div id="_section_36" class="pdq-sections">

1111<div class="key-points">

1112<h3 id="_36_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

1113Key Points</h3>

1114<div id="_kp_section_36_2">

1115<ul>

1116<li>

1117Childhood cancer survivors have an increased risk of a second cancer later in life.</li>

1118<li>

1119 Certain genetic patterns or syndromes may increase the risk of a second cancer.</li>

1120<li>

1121Patients who have been treated for cancer need regular screening tests to check for a second cancer.</li>

1122<li>

1123The kind of test used to screen for a second cancer depends in part on the kind of cancer treatment the patient had in the past.</li>

1124</ul>

1125</div>

1126</div>

1127<section id="_37">

1128<h3 id="_38" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1129Childhood cancer survivors have an increased risk of a second cancer later in life.</h3>

1130<p id="_484" tabindex="-1">

1131A different <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45847&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045847&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1132primary cancer</a>

1133 that occurs at least two months after <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1134cancer</a>

1135 treatment ends is called a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46658&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046658&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1136second cancer</a>

1137. A second cancer may occur months or years after treatment is completed. The type of second cancer that occurs depends in part on the original type of cancer and the cancer treatment. <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46079&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046079&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1138Benign tumors</a>

1139 (not cancer) may also occur. </p>

1140<p id="_517" tabindex="-1">

1141Second cancers that occur after cancer treatment include the following:</p>

1142<div class="pdq-content-list">

1143<ul id="_518">

1144<li>

1145<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45266&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045266&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1146Myelodysplastic syndrome</a>

1147 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46347&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046347&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1148acute myeloid leukemia</a>

1149.</li>

1150<li>

1151<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45301&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045301&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1152Solid tumors</a>

1153.</li>

1154</ul>

1155</div>

1156<p id="_959" tabindex="-1">

1157Myelodysplastic syndrome and acute myeloid leukemia may appear less than 10 years after a primary cancer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1158diagnosis</a>

1159 of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270800&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270800&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1160Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

1161, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45586&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045586&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1162acute lymphoblastic leukemia</a>

1163, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45562&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045562&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1164sarcoma</a>

1165, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=427310&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000427310&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1166central nervous system (CNS) tumor</a>

1167, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1168non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

1169, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45418&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045418&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1170neuroblastoma</a>

1171, or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45946&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045946&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1172Wilms tumor</a>

1173 and treatment with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45214&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045214&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1174chemotherapy</a>

1175 that included the following:</p>

1176<div class="pdq-content-list">

1177<ul id="_960">

1178<li>

1179An <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45589&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045589&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1199.</li>

1207</div>

1208<p id="_1000" tabindex="-1">

1209Patients treated with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1210radiation</a>

1398<p id="_43" tabindex="-1">

1399Some childhood cancer survivors may have an increased risk of developing a second cancer because they have a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=302456&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000302456&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1400family history</a>

1401 of cancer, an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45098&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045098&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1402inherited</a>

1403 cancer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45090&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045090&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1404syndrome</a>

1405 such as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46322&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046322&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1406Li-Fraumeni syndrome</a>

1407, or a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46391&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046391&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1408genetic</a>

1409 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46063&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046063&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1410mutation</a>

1411 such as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45096&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045096&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1412neurofibromatosis type 1</a>

1413. Problems with the way <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1416cells</a>

1417 and the way anticancer drugs are used by the body may also affect the risk of second cancers.</p>

1419<section id="_542">

1420<h3 id="_543" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1421Patients who have been treated for cancer need regular screening tests to check for a second cancer.</h3>

1422<p id="_544" tabindex="-1">

1423It is important for patients who have been treated for cancer to be checked for a second cancer before <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1424symptoms</a>

1425 appear. This is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46171&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046171&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1426screening</a>

1427 and may help find a second cancer at an early <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1428stage</a>

1429. When <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44636&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044636&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1430abnormal</a>

1431 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1432tissue</a>

1433 or cancer is found early, it may be easier to treat. By the time symptoms appear, cancer may have begun to spread.</p>

1434<p id="_545" tabindex="-1">

1435It is important to remember that your child's doctor does not necessarily think your child has cancer if he or she suggests a screening test. Screening tests are given when your child has no cancer symptoms.

1436

1437If a screening test result is abnormal, your child may need to have more tests done to find out if he or she has a second cancer. These are called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45959&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045959&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1438diagnostic tests</a>

1439.

1440

1441</p>

1442</section>

1443<section id="_546">

1444<h3 id="_547" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1445The kind of test used to screen for a second cancer depends in part on the kind of cancer treatment the patient had in the past.</h3>

1446<p id="_548" tabindex="-1">

1447All patients who have been treated for cancer should have a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1448physical exam</a>

1449 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=689078&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000689078&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1450medical history</a>

1451 done once a year. A physical exam of the body is done to check general <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1452signs</a>

1453 of health, including checking for signs of disease, such as lumps, changes in the skin, or anything else that seems unusual. A medical history is taken to learn about the patient&#8217;s health habits and past illnesses and treatments.</p>

1454<p id="_553" tabindex="-1">

1455If the patient received radiation therapy, the following tests and procedures may be used to check for <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=445084&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000445084&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1456skin</a>

1457, breast, or colorectal cancer:</p>

1458<div class="pdq-content-list">

1459<ul id="_554">

1460<li>

1461<strong>

1462Skin exam</strong>

1463: A doctor or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269445&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269445&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1464nurse</a>

1465 checks the skin for bumps or spots that look abnormal in color, size, shape, or texture, especially in the area where radiation was given.

1466It is suggested that a skin exam be done once a year to check for signs of skin cancer.</li>

1467<li>

1468<strong>

1469<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=304714&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000304714&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1470Breast self-exam</a>

1471</strong>

1472: An exam of the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=304766&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000304766&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1473breast</a>

1474 by the patient. The patient carefully feels the breasts and under the arms for lumps or anything else that seems unusual. It is suggested that women treated with a higher dose of radiation therapy to the chest do a monthly breast self-exam beginning at <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=440113&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000440113&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1475puberty</a>

1476. Women who were treated with a lower dose of radiation to the chest may not need to begin checking for breast cancer at puberty. Talk to your doctor about when you should begin breast self-exams.</li>

1477<li>

1478<strong>

1479<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=304715&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000304715&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1480Clinical breast exam</a>

1481 (CBE)</strong>

1482: An exam of the breast by a doctor or other health professional. The doctor will carefully feel the breasts and under the arms for lumps or anything else that seems unusual.

1483

1484It is suggested that women treated with a higher dose of radiation therapy to the chest have a clinical breast exam every year beginning at puberty until age 25. After age 25 or 8 years after radiation treatments end (whichever is first), clinical breast exams are done every 6 months. Women who were treated with a lower dose of radiation to the chest may not need to begin checking for breast cancer at puberty. Talk to your doctor about when you should begin clinical breast exams.</li>

1485<li>

1486<strong>

1487<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45775&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045775&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1488Mammogram</a>

1489</strong>

1490: An <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1491x-ray</a>

1492 of the breast. A mammogram may be done in women who had a higher dose of radiation to the chest and who do not have dense breasts.

1493

1494It is suggested that these women have a mammogram once a year starting 8 years after treatment or at age 25, whichever is later. Talk to your doctor about when you should begin to have mammograms to check for breast cancer.</li>

1495<li>

1496<strong>

1497Breast <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45788&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045788&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1498MRI</a>

1499 (magnetic resonance imaging)</strong>

1500: A procedure that uses a magnet, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1501radio waves</a>

1502, and a computer to make a series of detailed pictures of the breast. This procedure is also called nuclear magnetic resonance imaging (NMRI). An MRI may be done in women who had a higher dose of radiation to the chest and who have dense breasts. It is suggested that these women have an MRI once a year starting 8 years after treatment or at age 25, whichever is later. If you had radiation to the chest, talk to your doctor about whether you need an MRI of the breast to check for breast cancer.</li>

1503<li>

1504<strong>

1505<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45648&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045648&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1506Colonoscopy</a>

1507</strong>

1508: A procedure to look inside the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46555&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046555&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1509rectum</a>

1510 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1511colon</a>

1512 for polyps, abnormal areas, or cancer. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46463&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046463&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1513colonoscope</a>

1514 is inserted through the rectum into the colon. A colonoscope is a thin, tube-like instrument with a light and a lens for viewing. It may also have a tool to remove polyps or tissue samples, which are checked under a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1515microscope</a>

1516 for signs of cancer. It is suggested that childhood cancer survivors who had a higher dose of radiation to the abdomen, pelvis, or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=415914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000415914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1517spine</a>

1518 have a colonoscopy every 5 years. This begins at age 30 or 5 years after treatment ended, whichever is later. If you had radiation to the abdomen, pelvis, or spine, talk to your doctor about when you should begin to have colonoscopies to check for colorectal cancer.</li>

1519<li>

1520<strong>

1521Multitarget <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46605&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046605&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1522stool</a>

1523 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1524DNA</a>

1525 test</strong>

1526: A test to collect stool to check for cancer cells. This test may be done every 3 years beginning at age 30 or 5 years after treatment ended.</li>

1527</ul>

1536 <section id="_44">

1537

1538 <h2>

1539Cardiovascular System</h2>

1540

1541 <div id="_section_44" class="pdq-sections">

1542<div class="key-points">

1543<h3 id="_44_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

1544Key Points</h3>

1545<div id="_kp_section_44_3">

1546<ul>

1547<li>

1548Heart and blood vessel late effects are more likely to occur after treatment for certain childhood cancers.</li>

1549<li>

1550Radiation to the chest and certain types of chemotherapy increase the risk of heart and blood vessel late effects.</li>

1551<li>

1552Late effects that affect the heart and blood vessels may cause certain health problems.</li>

1553<li>

1554Childhood cancer survivors may have late effects that affect the heart during pregnancy.</li>

1555<li>

1556Possible signs and symptoms of heart and blood vessel late effects include trouble breathing and chest pain.

1557

1558</li>

1559<li>

1560Certain tests and procedures are used to diagnose health problems in the heart and blood vessels.

1561

1562</li>

1563<li>

1564Health habits that promote a healthy heart and blood vessels are important for survivors of childhood cancer.</li>

1565</ul>

1566</div>

1567</div>

1599Head and neck cancer</a>

1773<h3 id="_974" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1774Childhood cancer survivors may have late effects that affect the heart during pregnancy.</h3>

1775<p id="_975" tabindex="-1">

1776Long-term <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=450125&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000450125&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1777survivors</a>

1778 of childhood, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=776825&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000776825&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1779adolescent</a>

1780, and young adult cancers who have received radiation therapy or certain types of chemotherapy are at risk of a rare type of heart failure during <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=666677&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000666677&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1781pregnancy</a>

1782 called peripartum cardiomyopathy (PPCM). It may occur during late pregnancy and up to 5 months after giving birth. Patients at risk of this <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1783condition</a>

1787<h3 id="_563" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1788Possible signs and symptoms of heart and blood vessel late effects include trouble breathing and chest pain.

1789

1790</h3>

1791<p id="_564" tabindex="-1">

1792These and other <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1793signs</a>

1794 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1795symptoms</a>

1796 may be caused by heart and blood vessel late effects or by other <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1797conditions</a>

1798:</p>

1799<div class="pdq-content-list">

1800<ul id="_565">

1801<li>

1802Trouble breathing, especially when lying down.

1803</li>

1804<li>

1805Heartbeat that is too slow, too fast, or different from the heart's normal rhythm.

1806</li>

1807<li>

1808Chest pain or pain in the arm or leg.</li>

1809<li>

1810Swelling of the feet, ankles, legs, or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1811abdomen</a>

1812.</li>

1813<li>

1814When exposed to cold or having strong emotions, the fingers, toes, ears, or nose become white and then turn blue. When this happens to the fingers, there may also be pain and tingling. </li>

1815<li>

1816Sudden numbness or weakness of the face, arm, or leg (especially on one side of the body).</li>

1817<li>

1818Sudden <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=450096&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000450096&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1819confusion</a>

1820 or trouble speaking or understanding speech.</li>

1821<li>

1822Sudden trouble seeing with one or both eyes.</li>

1823<li>

1824Sudden trouble walking or feeling dizzy.</li>

1825<li>

1826Sudden loss of balance or coordination.</li>

1827<li>

1828Sudden severe headache for no known reason.</li>

1829<li>

1831</ul>

1832</div>

1833<p id="_569" tabindex="-1">

1835</section>

1836<section id="_557">

1837<h3 id="_558" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1838Certain tests and procedures are used to diagnose health problems in the heart and blood vessels.

1839

1840</h3>

1841<p id="_1001" tabindex="-1">

1842In addition to asking about your child's personal and family <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=798522&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000798522&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1843health history</a>

1844 and doing a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1845physical exam</a>

1846, your child's doctor may perform the following tests and procedures.</p>

1847<div class="pdq-content-list">

1848<ul id="_560">

1849<li>

1850<strong>

1851<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=635410&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000635410&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1852Electrocardiogram</a>

1853 (EKG)</strong>

1854: A recording of the heart's electrical activity to check its rate and rhythm. A number of small pads (electrodes) are placed on the patient&#8217;s chest, arms, and legs, and are connected by wires to the EKG machine. Heart activity is then recorded as a line graph on paper. Electrical activity that is faster or slower than normal may be a sign of heart disease or damage.</li>

1855<li>

1856<strong>

1857<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46032&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046032&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1858Echocardiogram</a>

1859</strong>

1860: A procedure in which high-energy sound waves (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46157&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046157&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1861ultrasound</a>

1862) are bounced off the heart and nearby <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1863tissues</a>

1864 or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1865organs</a>

1866 and make echoes. A moving picture is made of the heart and heart valves as blood is pumped through the heart.</li>

1867<li>

1868<strong>

1869Ultrasound exam</strong>

1870: A procedure in which high-energy sound waves (ultrasound) are bounced off internal tissues or organs such as the heart and make echoes. The echoes form a picture of body tissues called a sonogram. The picture can be printed to be looked at later.

1871

1872</li>

1873<li>

1874<strong>

1875<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45788&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045788&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1876MRI</a>

1877 (magnetic resonance imaging)</strong>

1878: A procedure that uses a magnet, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1879radio waves</a>

1880, and a computer to make a series of detailed pictures of areas inside the body. This procedure is also called nuclear magnetic resonance imaging (NMRI). This procedure is done to check for <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476017&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476017&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1881blood clots</a>

1882.</li>

1883<li>

1884<strong>

1885<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1886CT scan</a>

1887 (CAT scan)</strong>

1888: A procedure that makes a series of detailed pictures of areas inside the body, taken from different angles. The pictures are made by a computer linked to an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1889x-ray</a>

1890 machine. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=409764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000409764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1891dye</a>

1892 may be <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1893injected</a>

1894 into a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1895vein</a>

1896 or swallowed to help the organs or tissues show up more clearly. This procedure is also called computed tomography, computerized tomography, or computerized axial tomography. This procedure is done to check for blood clots.</li>

1897<li>

1898<strong>

1899<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=732555&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000732555&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1900MRA</a>

1901 (magnetic resonance angiography)</strong>

1902: A procedure that uses radio waves and a powerful magnet linked to a computer to create detailed pictures of the blood vessels and blood flow inside the body. A dye may be injected into a vein to make the blood vessels and blood flow easier to see. This may be used to check for blood clots or other blood vessel problems.</li>

1903<li>

1904<strong>

1905<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46068&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046068&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1906Lipid</a>

1907 profile studies</strong>

1908: A procedure in which a blood sample is checked to measure the amounts of triglycerides, cholesterol, and low- and high-density lipoprotein cholesterol

1909

1910in the blood.</li>

1911</ul>

1912</div>

1913<p id="_570" tabindex="-1">

1914Talk to your child's doctor about whether your child needs to have tests and procedures to check for signs of heart and blood vessel late effects. If tests are needed, find out how often they should be done.</p>

1915</section>

1916<section id="_840">

1917<h3 id="_841" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1918Health habits that promote a healthy heart and blood vessels are important for survivors of childhood cancer.</h3>

1919<p id="_842" tabindex="-1">

1920Childhood cancer survivors may lower their risk of heart and blood vessel late effects by having a healthy lifestyle, which includes:</p>

1921<div class="pdq-content-list">

1922<ul id="_843">

1923<li>

1924A healthy weight.</li>

1925<li>

1926A heart-healthy <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44660&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044660&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1927diet</a>

1928.</li>

1929<li>

1930Regular exercise.</li>

1931<li>

1932Not smoking.</li>

1933</ul>

1934</div>

1944 <h2>

1945Central Nervous System</h2>

1946

1947 <div id="_section_493" class="pdq-sections">

1948<div class="key-points">

1949<h3 id="_493_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

1950Key Points</h3>

1951<div id="_kp_section_493_4">

1952<ul>

1953<li>

1954Brain and spinal cord late effects are more likely to occur after treatment for certain childhood cancers.</li>

1955<li>

1956Radiation to the brain increases the risk of brain and spinal cord late effects.</li>

1957<li>

1958Late effects that affect the brain and spinal cord may cause certain health problems.</li>

1959<li>

1960Possible signs and symptoms of brain and spinal cord late effects include headaches, loss of coordination, and seizures.</li>

1961<li>

1962Certain tests and procedures are used to diagnose health problems in the brain and spinal cord.</li>

1963<li>

1964Survivors of childhood cancer may have anxiety and depression related to their cancer.</li>

1965<li>

1966Some childhood cancer survivors have post-traumatic stress disorder.</li>

1967<li>

1968Adolescents who are diagnosed with cancer may have social problems later in life.</li>

1969</ul>

1970</div>

1971</div>

2023<h3 id="_500" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

2024Radiation to the brain increases the risk of brain and spinal cord late effects.</h3>

2025<p id="_501" tabindex="-1">

2026The risk of health problems that affect the brain or spinal cord increases after treatment with the following:</p>

2027<div class="pdq-content-list">

2028<ul id="_502">

2029<li>

2030<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2031Radiation</a>

2032 to the brain or spinal cord, especially <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=440106&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000440106&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2033high doses of radiation</a>

2034. This includes <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2035total-body irradiation</a>

2036 given as part of a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46695&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046695&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2037stem cell transplant</a>

2038.</li>

2039<li>

2040<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46681&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046681&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

This includes <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=346522&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000346522&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2105<p id="_961" tabindex="-1">

2106<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46481&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046481&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2107Central nervous system</a>
